      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Delaware Valley
       </b>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">
        valley
       </a>
       through which the
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">
        Delaware River
       </a>
       flows. By extension, this
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponym" title="Toponym">
        toponym
       </a>
       is commonly used to refer to
       <b>
        Greater Philadelphia
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        Philadelphia metropolitan area
       </b>
       ("the [Lower] Delaware Valley Metropolitan Area"), which straddles the Lower Delaware River just north of
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">
        its estuary
       </a>
       . The Delaware Valley Metropolitan Area is located at the southern part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">
        Northeast megalopolis
       </a>
       and as such, the Delaware Valley can be described as either a
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">
        metropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (MSA), or as a broader
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       (CSA). The Delaware Valley Metropolitan Area is composed of several counties in southeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
        Pennsylvania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/South_Jersey" title="South Jersey">
        southwestern New Jersey
       </a>
       , one county in
       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">
        northern Delaware
       </a>
       and one county in
       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_County,_Maryland" title="Cecil County, Maryland">
        northeastern Maryland
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        MSA
       </a>
       has a population of over 6 million, while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">
        CSA
       </a>
       has a population of over 7.1 million (as of the 2010 Census Bureau count).
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
        Philadelphia
       </a>
       , being the region's major commercial, cultural, and industrial center, wields a rather large sphere of influence that affects the counties that immediately surround it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the Delaware Valley's most well-known contributions to human civilization involve the region's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Boston" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston">
        higher education
       </a>
       and medical institutions. The Delaware Valley has been influential upon American
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">
        history
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States" title="Economy of the United States">
        industry
       </a>
       . The region are leaders in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higher_Education" title="Higher Education">
        higher education
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
        biotechnology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">
        medicine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourism
       </a>
       and many others. With a gross domestic product of $388 billion, Philadelphia ranks ninth among world cities and fourth in the nation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area has hosted many people and sites significant to
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">
        American culture
       </a>
       and history, particularly in
       <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">
        the arts
       </a>
       , where Philadelphia alone has more outdoor
       <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">
        sculptures
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">
        murals
       </a>
       than any other American city,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">
        politics
       </a>
       , including many influential people involved in politics such as
       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">
        Benjamin Franklin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">
        Joe Biden
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
        American Revolution
       </a>
       . Philadelphia is famously known as "The Birthplace of America"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">
        Declaration of Independence
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">
        Constitution
       </a>
       were both drafted and signed there. On December 7, 1787,
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">
        Delaware
       </a>
       became the first state to ratify the Constitution, and has since promoted itself as
       <i>
        "The First State"
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Delaware Valley was home to many other instrumental moments in the American Revolution, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">
        First
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">
        Second Continental Congress
       </a>
       , the preservation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Bell#Early_days_(1754–1846)" title="Liberty Bell">
        Liberty Bell
       </a>
       , the Battles of
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Germantown" title="Battle of Germantown">
        Germantown
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Brandywine" title="Battle of Brandywine">
        Brandywine
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Red_Bank" title="Battle of Red Bank">
        Red Bank
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Mifflin" title="Siege of Fort Mifflin">
        Siege of Fort Mifflin
       </a>
       , the winter of 1777–78 at
       <a href="/wiki/Valley_Forge" title="Valley Forge">
        Valley Forge
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(United_States)" title="Constitutional Convention (United States)">
        Philadelphia Convention
       </a>
       , and many others. Philadelphia was one of the nation's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States" title="List of capitals in the United States">
        capitals
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
        Revolutionary War
       </a>
       , and served as temporary U.S. capital while
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington, D.C.
       </a>
       , was under construction.
      </p>
      <p>
       Today, the area is home to some of the most prestigious universities in the world, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">
        University of Pennsylvania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">
        Drexel University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Villanova_University" title="Villanova University">
        Villanova University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph's University">
        Saint Joseph's University
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">
        Temple University
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">
        Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania
       </a>
       is consistently ranked as the best business school in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DelawareRiverBasin-01.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1830" data-file-width="1578" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DelawareRiverBasin-01.png/200px-DelawareRiverBasin-01.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DelawareRiverBasin-01.png/300px-DelawareRiverBasin-01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/DelawareRiverBasin-01.png/400px-DelawareRiverBasin-01.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DelawareRiverBasin-01.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The drainage basin of the Delaware River.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In geology and geography, a strict sense of the term would incorporate the Delaware River's main
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">
        drainage basin
       </a>
       , and so encompass major tributaries such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Schuylkill_River" title="Schuylkill River">
        Schuylkill River
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_River" title="Lehigh River">
        Lehigh River
       </a>
       and their valleys or sub-basins. These extensions also apply culturally with decreasing degree gradually decreased by proximal distance because the ease of land travel enables a great deal of daily interaction; for example, the large number of commuters who travel daily 45–90 minutes creates cultural blends and parallel values.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the course of their work, U.S. government agencies have reached various definitions of the Delaware Valley and the Greater Philadelphia Area. The
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Valley_Regional_Planning_Commission" title="Delaware Valley Regional Planning Commission">
        Delaware Valley Regional Planning Commission
       </a>
       (DVRPC) serves Philadelphia, four suburban
       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
        Pennsylvania
       </a>
       counties (
       <a href="/wiki/Bucks_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Bucks County, Pennsylvania">
        Bucks County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chester_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester County, Pennsylvania">
        Chester County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Delaware County, Pennsylvania">
        Delaware County
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Montgomery County, Pennsylvania">
        Montgomery County
       </a>
       ), and four
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       counties (
       <a href="/wiki/Burlington_County,_New_Jersey" title="Burlington County, New Jersey">
        Burlington County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Camden_County,_New_Jersey" title="Camden County, New Jersey">
        Camden County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County,_New_Jersey" title="Gloucester County, New Jersey">
        Gloucester County
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mercer_County,_New_Jersey" title="Mercer County, New Jersey">
        Mercer County
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvrpc1_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dvrpc1-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
        Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       (OMB) defines
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">
        metropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (MSAs), which are regions with relatively high population densities at their cores and close economic ties throughout their respective areas. Philadelphia is located in the Philadelphia-Camden-Wilmington Metropolitan Statistical Area, which includes all of the counties served by the DVRPC except for Mercer County, and also includes
       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">
        New Castle County, Delaware
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_County,_Maryland" title="Cecil County, Maryland">
        Cecil County, Maryland
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Salem_County,_New_Jersey" title="Salem County, New Jersey">
        Salem County, New Jersey
       </a>
       . The OMB also groups one or more MSAs into larger
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical areas
       </a>
       (CSAs), which reflect commuting patterns. MSAs and CSAs are not formal administrative divisions, but serve as useful tools for understanding the extent of metropolitan areas such as the Delaware Valley. The Philadelphia-Reading-Camden Combined Statistical Area includes all of the counties from the Philadelphia-Camden-Wilmington Metropolitan Statistical Area, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Berks_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Berks County, Pennsylvania">
        Berks County, Pennsylvania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Delaware" title="Kent County, Delaware">
        Kent County, Delaware
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_County,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic County, New Jersey">
        Atlantic County, New Jersey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_May_County,_New_Jersey" title="Cape May County, New Jersey">
        Cape May County, New Jersey
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_County,_New_Jersey" title="Cumberland County, New Jersey">
        Cumberland County, New Jersey
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_economy">
        Population and economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Population and economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       According to 2016 estimates from the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">
        United States Census Bureau
       </a>
       , the Philadelphia-Camden-Wilmington Metropolitan Statistical Area ranks as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
        seventh-largest MSA
       </a>
       in the United States with 6,070,500 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">
        Bureau of Economic Analysis
       </a>
       , the Philadelphia-Camden-Wilmington MSA had a
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        gross domestic product
       </a>
       of $431 billion, the ninth-largest among U.S. metropolitan areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       2016 Census Bureau estimates rank the Philadelphia-Reading-Camden Combined Statistical Area as the ninth-largest CSA in the United States, with 7,179,357 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCSA_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstCSA-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Philadelphia Philadelphia-Camden-Wilmington Metropolitan Statistical Area's population of roughly 6 million people is comparable to that of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_(United_Nations)" title="List of countries by population (United Nations)">
        countries
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
        Denmark
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       . The MSA's nominal gross domestic product of $431 billion is comparable to
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">
        countries
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">
        Thailand
       </a>
       . The MSA also ranks as the second most populous in the
       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">
        Northeastern United States
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">
        New York metropolitan area
       </a>
       , while the CSA is third-largest in the Northeast after the New York and
       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
        Boston
       </a>
       metropolitan areas. The
       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area">
        Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area
       </a>
       , which is part of Northeast Megalopolis but is considered part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">
        Southeastern United States
       </a>
       under Census Bureau definitions, is also larger than the Philadelphia metropolitan area. Philadelphia itself is the sixth-most populous city in the United States and the third-most populous U.S. city east of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       , after
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       . Philadelphia's
       <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">
        media market
       </a>
       ranks fourth, behind New York City,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_area" title="Greater Los Angeles area">
        Los Angeles
       </a>
       , and Chicago, in
       <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">
        Nielsen
       </a>
       Media Market
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_television_markets" title="List of United States television markets">
        size rankings
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Such educational institutions as
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Valley_Regional_High_School" title="Delaware Valley Regional High School">
        Delaware Valley Regional High School
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Alexandria Township, New Jersey">
        Alexandria Township
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_Valley_College" title="Delaware Valley College">
        Delaware Valley College
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Doylestown_Township,_Bucks_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Doylestown Township, Bucks County, Pennsylvania">
        Doylestown Township
       </a>
       are named after the region. Likewise,
       <a href="/wiki/Frenchtown,_New_Jersey" title="Frenchtown, New Jersey">
        Frenchtown's
       </a>
       now defunct newspaper
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hunterdon_County_Democrat" title="The Hunterdon County Democrat">
        <i>
         The Delaware Valley News
        </i>
       </a>
       was another example of the usage.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Subregions">
        Subregions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Subregions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas_of_New_Jersey" title="Metropolitan Statistical Areas of New Jersey">
        Metropolitan Statistical Areas of New Jersey
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Sixteen counties in four states constitute the Philadelphia-Reading-Camden Combined Statistical Area. The five Pennsylvania counties in the MSA are collectively known as
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Pennsylvania" title="Regions of Pennsylvania">
        Southeastern Pennsylvania
       </a>
       , and the four suburban counties from this region are sometimes called the "collar counties."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collarcounties1_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-collarcounties1-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Aside from Philadelphia, major municipalities in Southeastern Pennsylvania include the
       <a href="/wiki/Inner_suburb" title="Inner suburb">
        inner suburbs
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Darby_Township,_Delaware_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Upper Darby Township, Delaware County, Pennsylvania">
        Upper Darby Township
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bensalem_Township,_Pennsylvania" title="Bensalem Township, Pennsylvania">
        Bensalem Township
       </a>
       . Berks County, which forms its own MSA and contains the CSA's second largest city,
       <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">
        Reading
       </a>
       , is generally not considered to be part of Southeastern Pennsylvania and is sometimes assigned to
       <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Pennsylvania" title="South Central Pennsylvania">
        South Central Pennsylvania
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The seven New Jersey counties in the CSA form
       <a href="/wiki/South_Jersey" title="South Jersey">
        South Jersey
       </a>
       , although
       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_County,_New_Jersey" title="Ocean County, New Jersey">
        Ocean County
       </a>
       , which is part of the New York CSA, is also sometimes considered to be part of South Jersey.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sstirling1_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sstirling1-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Atlantic County, Cape May County, and Cumberland County each form their own respective metropolitan statistical areas.
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">
        Atlantic City
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Shore" title="Jersey Shore">
        Jersey Shore
       </a>
       are major tourist destinations for people from inside and outside of the Delaware Valley. Other major municipalities in South Jersey include
       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hill,_New_Jersey" title="Cherry Hill, New Jersey">
        Cherry Hill
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">
        Camden
       </a>
       , which is across the Delaware River from Philadelphia.
      </p>
      <p>
       The two counties of Delaware in the CSA constitute a majority of Delaware's land mass and population.
       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">
        Wilmington
       </a>
       is the most populous city in Delaware and the fifth-most populous municipality in the Delaware Valley. The lone Maryland county in the Philadelphia-Reading-Camden Combined Statistical Area is part of the region known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">
        Eastern Shore of Maryland
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Although Mercer County in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Jersey" title="Central Jersey">
        Central Jersey
       </a>
       is often considered part of the Delaware Valley from a cultural perspective, it is classified as part of New York's CSA by the OMB. Mercer County and two counties in Pennsylvania's
       <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley" title="Lehigh Valley">
        Lehigh Valley
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Lehigh County, Pennsylvania">
        Lehigh County
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northampton_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Northampton County, Pennsylvania">
        Northampton County
       </a>
       , are part of the Philadelphia media market.
       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_County,_Maryland" title="Caroline County, Maryland">
        Caroline County, Maryland
       </a>
       is also part of the Philadelphia media market.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-truckadsmarkets_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-truckadsmarkets-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">
        Characteristics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Characteristics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3009" data-file-width="2006" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG/175px-Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG/263px-Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG/350px-Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG 2x" width="175"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duffys_Cut_Cross_West_Laurel_Hill.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Grave of some of the 57 Irish victims of
         <a href="/wiki/Duffy%27s_Cut" title="Duffy's Cut">
          Duffy's Cut
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/West_Laurel_Hill_Cemetery" title="West Laurel Hill Cemetery">
          West Laurel Hill Cemetery
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Bala_Cynwyd,_Pennsylvania" title="Bala Cynwyd, Pennsylvania">
          Bala Cynwyd, Pennsylvania
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Irish_Americans_in_Philadelphia" title="History of the Irish Americans in Philadelphia">
          Irish Americans
         </a>
         make up the largest ethnicity in the Delaware Valley.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Philadelphia_21-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Global_Philadelphia-21">
           [21]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2245" data-file-width="2302" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg/220px-Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg/330px-Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg/440px-Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Friendship_Gate_Chinatown_Philadelphia_from_east.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Philadelphia's
         <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Philadelphia" title="Chinatown, Philadelphia">
          Chinatown
         </a>
         is home to many Chinese and other Asian restaurants.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westchester.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westchester.jpg/220px-Westchester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westchester.jpg/330px-Westchester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Westchester.jpg/440px-Westchester.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westchester.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/West_Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="West Chester, Pennsylvania">
          West Chester, Pennsylvania
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Delaware Valley is home to extensive populations of
       <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">
        Irish Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">
        German Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">
        English Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Americans" title="Ukrainian Americans">
        Ukrainian Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">
        Italian Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish-Americans" title="Swedish-Americans">
        Swedish-Americans
       </a>
       (which have a museum located at FDR Park in South Philadelphia),
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_Americans" title="Polish Americans">
        Polish Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Americans" title="Scottish Americans">
        Scottish Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_Americans" title="Scotch-Irish Americans">
        Scotch-Irish Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_Americans" title="Greek Americans">
        Greek Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">
        African Americans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
        Asians
       </a>
       such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_American" title="Chinese American">
        Chinese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_American" title="Indian American">
        Indian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">
        Korean
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_American" title="Vietnamese American">
        Vietnamese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian-American" title="Armenian-American">
        Armenians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
        Arabs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">
        Turks
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Pakistanis" title="Pakistanis">
        Pakistanis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Israelis" title="Israelis">
        Israelis
       </a>
       (while
       <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">
        American Jews
       </a>
       form a significant ethno-religious community),
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanics
       </a>
       . Within the Hispanic population, the vast majority are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stateside_Puerto_Ricans" title="Stateside Puerto Ricans">
        Puerto Ricans
       </a>
       , though other groups include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">
        Dominicans
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">
        Mexicans
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is a significant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" title="West Indian American">
        West Indian
       </a>
       community. There is even a small
       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
        Native American
       </a>
       community known as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Lenapehoking" title="Lenapehoking">
         Lenapehoking
        </a>
       </i>
       for Lenni-
       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">
        Lenape
       </a>
       Indians of
       <a href="/wiki/West_Philadelphia" title="West Philadelphia">
        West Philadelphia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Philadelphia's suburbs contain a high concentration of malls, the two largest of which have at least 5,000,000 square feet (460,000 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of office space, and at least 600,000 square feet (56,000 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of retail. These are the
       <a href="/wiki/King_of_Prussia_Mall" title="King of Prussia Mall">
        King of Prussia Mall
       </a>
       in King of Prussia, Pennsylvania, which is the largest in the United States (leasable sq. feet of retail space), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hill_Mall" title="Cherry Hill Mall">
        Cherry Hill Mall
       </a>
       in Cherry Hill, New Jersey, which was the first enclosed mall on the East Coast. Malls, office complexes, strip shopping plazas, expressways, and tract housing are common sights, and more and more continue to replace rolling countryside, farms, woods, and wetlands. However, due to strong opposition by residents and political officials, many acres of land have been preserved throughout the Delaware Valley. Older townships and large boroughs such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Township,_PA" title="Cheltenham Township, PA">
        Cheltenham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Norristown,_Pennsylvania" title="Norristown, Pennsylvania">
        Norristown
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jenkintown,_Pennsylvania" title="Jenkintown, Pennsylvania">
        Jenkintown
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Darby,_Pennsylvania" title="Upper Darby, Pennsylvania">
        Upper Darby
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/West_Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="West Chester, Pennsylvania">
        West Chester
       </a>
       retain distinct community identities while engulfed in suburbia. The fastest-growing counties
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2012)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Chester_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester County, Pennsylvania">
        Chester
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Montgomery County, Pennsylvania">
        Montgomery
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bucks_County" title="Bucks County">
        Bucks
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County,_New_Jersey" title="Gloucester County, New Jersey">
        Gloucester
       </a>
       . Upper Darby, in
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Delaware County, Pennsylvania">
        Delaware County
       </a>
       is the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Township" title="Township">
        township
       </a>
       in the United States.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Sometimes
       <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Pennsylvania" title="Reading, Pennsylvania">
        Reading
       </a>
       is included in the Delaware Valley Metro Area.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_American_English" title="Mid-Atlantic American English">
        Mid-Atlantic American English
       </a>
       and its subset,
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_English" title="Philadelphia English">
        Philadelphia English
       </a>
       , are two common dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">
        American English
       </a>
       in Philadelphia and the Delaware Valley.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Delaware Valley has four distinct seasons with ample precipitation and is divided by the 0 °C (32 °F) January
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isotherm_(contour_line)" title="Isotherm (contour line)">
        isotherm
       </a>
       . Most of Philadelphia and the NJ portion, almost all of the DE and MD portions, part of Delaware County, and extreme southern portions of Bucks and Chester Counties have a
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
        humid subtropical climate
       </a>
       (
       <b>
        Cfa
       </b>
       .) The remainder of the Delaware Valley has a hot-summer
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        humid continental climate
       </a>
       (
       <b>
        Dfa
       </b>
       .) Snow amounts may vary widely year-to-year and normally do vary widely within the Delaware Valley. The region has only two ski areas:
       <a href="/wiki/Bear_Creek_Ski_and_Recreation_Area" title="Bear Creek Ski and Recreation Area">
        Bear Creek Ski and Recreation Area
       </a>
       in eastern Berks County and Spring Mountain in central Montgomery County.
      </p>
      <p>
       Using the -3 °C January isotherm as a boundary, all of the Delaware Valley is humid subtropical except for portions of Berks County and higher areas of northern Chester County. The warm-summer humid continental climate (
       <b>
        Dfb
       </b>
       ) only exists in higher areas of Berks where all monthly temperatures average below 22 °C.
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_history">
        Colonial history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Colonial history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">
        Thirteen Colonies
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Philadelphia" title="History of Philadelphia">
        History of Philadelphia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The valley was the territory of the
       <a href="/wiki/Susquehannock" title="Susquehannock">
        Susquehannock
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">
        Lenape
       </a>
       , who are recalled in place names throughout the region. The region became part of the Dutch colony of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">
        New Netherland
       </a>
       after the exploration of
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">
        Delaware Bay
       </a>
       in 1609. The Dutch called the
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">
        Delaware River
       </a>
       the
       <i>
        Zuyd Rivier
       </i>
       , or South River, and considered the lands along it banks and those of its
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">
        bay
       </a>
       to be the southern flank of its province of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">
        New Netherland
       </a>
       . In 1638, it began to be settled by Swedes, Forest Finns, Dutch, and
       <a href="/wiki/Walloons" title="Walloons">
        Walloons
       </a>
       and became the colony of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Sweden" title="New Sweden">
        New Sweden
       </a>
       , though this was not officially recognized by the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">
        Dutch Empire
       </a>
       which re-asserted control in 1655. The area was taken by the
       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">
        English
       </a>
       in 1664.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The name Delaware comes from
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_West,_3rd_Baron_De_La_Warr" title="Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr">
        Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr
       </a>
       , who had arrived at
       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">
        Jamestown, Virginia
       </a>
       in 1610, just as original settlers were about to abandon it, and thus maintaining the English foothold on the
       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
        North American
       </a>
       continent.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Many residents commute to jobs in
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
        Philadelphia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">
        Camden
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">
        Wilmington
       </a>
       with the help of
       <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">
        expressways
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Train" title="Train">
        trains
       </a>
       . Commutes from one suburb to another are also common, as office parks have sprung up in new commercial centers such as
       <a href="/wiki/King_of_Prussia,_Pennsylvania" title="King of Prussia, Pennsylvania">
        King of Prussia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Washington,_Pennsylvania" title="Fort Washington, Pennsylvania">
        Fort Washington
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cherry_Hill_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Cherry Hill Township, New Jersey">
        Cherry Hill
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Meeting,_Pennsylvania" title="Plymouth Meeting, Pennsylvania">
        Plymouth Meeting
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commuter_rail">
        Commuter rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Commuter rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Formerly, the region was served by the
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Valley_Railway" title="Delaware Valley Railway">
        Delaware Valley Railway
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thirty_St_Station.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Thirty_St_Station.jpg/220px-Thirty_St_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Thirty_St_Station.jpg/330px-Thirty_St_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Thirty_St_Station.jpg/440px-Thirty_St_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thirty_St_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Philadelphia's 30th St. Station has SEPTA Regional Rail and Amtrak service
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/SEPTA_Regional_Rail" title="SEPTA Regional Rail">
         SEPTA Regional Rail
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Airport_Line_(SEPTA)" title="Airport Line (SEPTA)">
           Airport Line
          </a>
          connecting Central Philadelphia with
          <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">
           Philadelphia International Airport
          </a>
          in Philadelphia and Delaware Counties.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Wilmington/Newark_Line" title="Wilmington/Newark Line">
           Wilmington/Newark Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia to the Wilmington, DE area (with limited weekday service to Newark, DE), via Chester City and Delaware County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Warminster_Line" title="Warminster Line">
           Warminster Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia with southeastern Montgomery County and Warminster in Bucks County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/West_Trenton_Line_(SEPTA)" title="West Trenton Line (SEPTA)">
           West Trenton Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia north to the Trenton, NJ area, serving Montgomery and Bucks County, PA between Jenkintown, PA and Yardley, PA, with the final stop in Ewing, NJ.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Media/Elwyn_Line" title="Media/Elwyn Line">
           Media/Elwyn Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia to central Delaware County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Paoli/Thorndale_Line" title="Paoli/Thorndale Line">
           Paoli/Thorndale Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia with the affluent Main Line area and western Chester County near Coatesville.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Lansdale/Doylestown_Line" title="Lansdale/Doylestown Line">
           Lansdale/Doylestown Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia with Lansdale in central Montgomery County and Doylestown in Bucks County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Manayunk/Norristown_Line" title="Manayunk/Norristown Line">
           Manayunk/Norristown Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia with Conshohocken and Norristown in Montgomery County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Cynwyd_Line" title="Cynwyd Line">
           Cynwyd Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia with Bala Cynwyd on the Philadelphia/Montgomery County line (limited weekday service)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Trenton_Line_(SEPTA)" title="Trenton Line (SEPTA)">
           Trenton Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia to Trenton, NJ, serving Bucks County.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Fox_Chase_Line" title="Fox Chase Line">
           Fox Chase Line
          </a>
          connecting Central Philadelphia with the Fox Chase area in Philadelphia.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_Hill_East_Line" title="Chestnut Hill East Line">
           Chestnut Hill East Line
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_Hill_West_Line" title="Chestnut Hill West Line">
           Chestnut Hill West Line
          </a>
          connecting Central Philadelphia with the Chestnut Hill area of the city.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit" title="New Jersey Transit">
         New Jersey Transit
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_Line" title="Atlantic City Line">
           Atlantic City Line
          </a>
          connecting Philadelphia to Atlantic City, NJ with connections to PATCO Speedline in Lindenwold, NJ.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Line_(New_Jersey_Transit)" title="River Line (New Jersey Transit)">
           River Line
          </a>
          connecting Camden (NJ) to Trenton (NJ) running along the east bank of the Delaware River.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/MARC_Train" title="MARC Train">
         MARC
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penn_Line_(MARC)" title="Penn Line (MARC)">
           Penn Line
          </a>
          connecting Perryville, MD to
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_MD" title="Baltimore, MD">
           Baltimore, MD
          </a>
          and
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." title="Washington D.C.">
           Washington D.C.
          </a>
          , and in the future will connect to SEPTA at Newark, DE.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Transit_Corporation" title="Port Authority Transit Corporation">
         PATCO
        </a>
        Speedline connecting Philadelphia to Lindenwold, NJ in Camden County with connections to NJT's Atlantic City Line.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_highways">
        Major highways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Major highways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <b>
        Major:
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">
         Philadelphia International Airport
        </a>
        (PHL), located 15 miles southwest of Center City Philadelphia, is the main international airport serving the immediate Delaware Valley Area
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">
         Newark Liberty International Airport
        </a>
        (EWR), while not in the Delaware Valley, is a major airport serving certain regions of the Delaware Valley, including
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bucks_County" title="Bucks County">
         Bucks County
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
         New Jersey
        </a>
        . It is located 60 miles northeast of Center City Philadelphia, and 25 miles northeast of Trenton.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <b>
        Secondary:
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley_International_Airport" title="Lehigh Valley International Airport">
         Lehigh Valley International Airport
        </a>
        (ABE)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Philadelphia_Airport" title="Northeast Philadelphia Airport">
         Northeast Philadelphia Airport
        </a>
        (PNE)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Castle_Airport" title="New Castle Airport">
         New Castle Airport
        </a>
        (ILG)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Reading_Regional_Airport" title="Reading Regional Airport">
         Reading Regional Airport
        </a>
        (RDG)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_International_Airport" title="Atlantic City International Airport">
         Atlantic City International Airport
        </a>
        (ACY)
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Philadelphia" title="Media in Philadelphia">
        Media in Philadelphia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The two main newspapers are
       <a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer">
        The Philadelphia Inquirer
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Daily_News" title="Philadelphia Daily News">
        Philadelphia Daily News
       </a>
       , owned by the
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Media_Network" title="Philadelphia Media Network">
        Philadelphia Media Network
       </a>
       . Local television channels include
       <a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">
        KYW-TV
       </a>
       3 (CBS),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPVI" title="WPVI">
        WPVI
       </a>
       6 (ABC),
       <a href="/wiki/WCAU" title="WCAU">
        WCAU
       </a>
       10 (NBC),
       <a href="/wiki/WHYY-TV" title="WHYY-TV">
        WHYY-TV
       </a>
       12 (PBS),
       <a href="/wiki/WPHL-TV" title="WPHL-TV">
        WPHL-TV
       </a>
       17 (MyNetworkTV),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTXF" title="WTXF">
        WTXF
       </a>
       29 (FOX),
       <a href="/wiki/WPSG" title="WPSG">
        WPSG
       </a>
       57 (CW), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPPX" title="WPPX">
        WPPX
       </a>
       61 (
       <a href="/wiki/Ion_Television" title="Ion Television">
        Ion
       </a>
       ). Radio stations serving the area include:
       <a href="/wiki/WRTI" title="WRTI">
        WRTI
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/WIOQ" title="WIOQ">
        WIOQ
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/WDAS_(AM)" title="WDAS (AM)">
        WDAS (AM)
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/WTEL_(AM)" title="WTEL (AM)">
        WTEL
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Area_codes">
        Area codes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Area codes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_codes_215_and_267" title="Area codes 215 and 267">
         215/267
        </a>
        : The City of Philadelphia and some of its northern suburbs
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Area_codes_610_and_484" title="Area codes 610 and 484">
         610/484
        </a>
        : Southeastern Pennsylvania outside Philadelphia, including the western suburbs, the Lehigh Valley, and most of Berks County
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Area_code_856" title="Area code 856">
         856
        </a>
        : Southwestern New Jersey, including Camden, Cherry Hill, and Vineland
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Area_code_609" title="Area code 609">
         609
        </a>
        : Central and Southeastern New Jersey, including Trenton, Atlantic City and the Jersey Shore
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Area_code_302" title="Area code 302">
         302
        </a>
        : Delaware
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Area_codes_410,_443,_and_667" title="Area codes 410, 443, and 667">
         410/443/667
        </a>
        : Eastern half of Maryland, including Cecil County
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_717" title="Area code 717">
         717
        </a>
        : South Central Pennsylvania, including Western Berks County
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Philadelphia itself is heavily
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic
       </a>
       , having voted for the Democratic candidate in every presidential election since
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1936" title="United States presidential election, 1936">
        1936
       </a>
       . The surrounding suburban counties are key political areas in Pennsylvania, which itself is an important
       <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">
        swing state
       </a>
       in federal politics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcohen1_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mcohen1-44">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       South Jersey has consistently voted Democratic at the presidential level in recent years, although the region is slightly more Republican-leaning than North Jersey and has voted for Republicans at the state and local level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cohennj_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cohennj-45">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Castle County's Democratic lean and large share of Delaware's population has tended to make Delaware as a whole vote for Democrats, while the less populous Kent County is more competitive.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cohende_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cohende-46">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recent well-known political figures from the Greater Philadelphia area include former Vice President
       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">
        Joe Biden
       </a>
       and former Pennsylvania Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Ed_Rendell" title="Ed Rendell">
        Ed Rendell
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Congressional_districts">
        Congressional districts
       </span>

       counties are not part of the CSA.

      <p>
       Additionally, the Delaware Valley is represented in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        United States Senate
       </a>
       by the eight Senators from Delaware, Maryland, New Jersey, and Pennsylvania.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lexicon_note">
        Lexicon note
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Lexicon note">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Some believe that the term "Delaware Valley" is not entirely a synonym for "Greater Philadelphia". "Greater Philadelphia" implies that the region is centered on the city in an economic and cultural context, while "Delaware Valley" is a more generic geographic term that does not imply that any part is of more consequence than any other. Several organizations, such as
       <a href="/wiki/KYW_(AM)" title="KYW (AM)">
        KYW Radio
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Philadelphia_Tourism_Marketing_Corporation" title="Greater Philadelphia Tourism Marketing Corporation">
        Greater Philadelphia Tourism Marketing Corporation
       </a>
       , consciously use the term "Greater Philadelphia" to assert that Philadelphia is the center of the region, referring to the less urbanized areas as "Philadelphia's countryside".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greater_Philadelphia_Tourism_Marketing_Corporation_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Greater_Philadelphia_Tourism_Marketing_Corporation-47">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Others note that the customary media usage of the term omits the majority of the length of the
       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">
        Delaware River
       </a>
       's valley that is not in metropolitan Philadelphia.
      </p>
      <p>
       WPVI-TV uses the slogan, "The Delaware Valley's leading news program" for their
       <a href="/wiki/Action_News" title="Action News">
        Action News
       </a>
       broadcast, since that program has led the ratings for news programs in the Philadelphia market for over 30 years.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delaware_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-23">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-23">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the highest and lowest temperature readings during an entire month or year) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-27">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-27">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Official temperature and precipitation measurements for Philadelphia were taken at the Weather Bureau Office in downtown from January 1872 to 19 June 1940, and at Philadelphia Int'l from 20 June 1940 to the present.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
            <a href="#cite_note-24">
             [23]
            </a>
           </sup>
           Snowfall and snow depth records date to 1 January 1884 and 1 October 1948, respectively.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhillyNOAA_25-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-PhillyNOAA-25">
             [24]
            </a>
           </sup>
           In 2006, snowfall measurements were moved to
           <a href="/wiki/National_Park,_New_Jersey" title="National Park, New Jersey">
            National Park, New Jersey
           </a>
           directly across the Delaware River from the airport.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
            <a href="#cite_note-26">
             [25]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-30">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-30">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the highest and lowest temperature readings during an entire month or year) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-32">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-32">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The official climatology station for Atlantic City was at the Weather Bureau Office downtown from January 1874 to 15 June 1958 and Atlantic City Int'l (ACY) in
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_Harbor_Township" title="Egg Harbor Township">
            Egg Harbor Township
           </a>
           since 16 June 1958.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
            <a href="#cite_note-31">
             [28]
            </a>
           </sup>
           ACY's location in the
           <a href="/wiki/Pine_Barrens_(New_Jersey)" title="Pine Barrens (New Jersey)">
            Pine Barrens
           </a>
           and distance away from the coast and
           <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">
            urban heat island
           </a>
           of downtown Atlantic City largely account for its markedly colder temperatures at night as compared to downtown; for example, from 1959 to 2013, there were 50 days with a low of 0 °F (−18 °C) or lower, while in the same period, the corresponding number of days at downtown was 2. The
           <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">
            National Weather Service
           </a>
           ceased regular snowfall observations at downtown after the winter of 1958–59.
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>

        <li id="cite_note-5">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-5">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">
           <a class="external text" href="https://learningenglish.voanews.com/a/nicknames-for-philadelphia-and-boston-89834907/112420.html" rel="nofollow">
            "Words and Their Stories: Nicknames for Philadelphia and Boston"
           </a>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">
            Voice of America
           </a>
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             July 11,
            </span>
            2017
           </span>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Words+and+Their+Stories%3A+Nicknames+for+Philadelphia+and+Boston&amp;rft.pub=Voice+of+America&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Flearningenglish.voanews.com%2Fa%2Fnicknames-for-philadelphia-and-boston-89834907%2F112420.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADelaware+Valley">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-6">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-6">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          "The First to Ratify" would be more accurate, as the beginnings of the states themselves date back to the Declaration of Independence, celebrated July 4, 1776, when what was to become the State of Delaware was still the three lower counties of Pennsylvania with the governor in Philadelphia, and not establishing independence from that body until
          <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Constitution_of_1776#Background" title="Delaware Constitution of 1776">
           September 20, 1776
          </a>
          . According to Delaware's own website, "Delaware became a state in 1776, just two months after the signing of the Declaration of Independence." (ref-
          <a class="external text" href="http://delaware.gov/facts/DelawareFactsandSymbols.pdf" rel="nofollow">
           pdf
          </a>
          ) Therefore Delaware was actually the
          <i>
           last
          </i>
          of the thirteen colonies to establish itself as a state. Additionally, the
          <a href="/wiki/50_State_Quarters#Designs" title="50 State Quarters">
           Delaware State Quarter
          </a>
          is minted with this nickname, yet shows
          <a href="/wiki/Caesar_Rodney#American_Revolution" title="Caesar Rodney">
           Caesar Rodney
          </a>
          on horseback in commemoration of how he was the
          <i>
           last
          </i>
          delegate to show up to the Continental Congress for the historic vote for independence. And with regard to the original Articles of Confederation, Delaware was the
          <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation#Ratification" title="Articles of Confederation">
           12th of the 13 states to ratify
          </a>
          .
         </span>
        </li>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">
        Further reading
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

        </span>
